Commentary
This passage defines a ruling and a category: the elite (khawass) are allowed to fast on the day of doubt, whereas the general public must not. The mufti, qadi, and those who have detailed knowledge of the rules of intention may fast as nafl. The key condition: they must be able to maintain a clear intention, free from doubt that the fast might be for Ramadan. They fast as nafl and do not mix it with Ramadan. The Urdu commentary elaborates that the elite understand the fiqh of intention and the conditions that make the fast valid.

Key Terms
الخواص (al-khawass): The elite: those with detailed knowledge of fiqh rules of fasting, able to avoid hesitation in intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the elite (muftis, qadis, and learned laypersons) to fast on the day of doubt as nafl, provided they can maintain a clear intention free from any ambiguity about Ramadan.

Sawm — Fasting

Solitary Crescent Sighting: Individual Obligation vs. Communal Authority
Ruling with proofs on crescent sighting and communal fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who sees the Shawwal crescent alone and explain the interplay between personal certainty and communal authority.

Core Idea
Personal certainty of the crescent does not permit breaking fast; communal practice binds the individual.

This lesson explores a critical tension in Hanafi fiqh between individual obligation and communal authority. When a person sees the Shawwal crescent on his own but the qadi rejects his testimony, is he allowed to break his fast? The passage presents the ruling, its proofs, and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The passage describes a person who sees the crescent of Shawwal (or Ramadan) alone, and the qadi does not accept his testimony. The ruling: he must continue fasting with the community and cannot break fast based on his certainty.
This applies whether he sees Ramadan or Shawwal crescent; the obligation is to follow communal practice.
2
Examine the first proof (individual obligation)
The hadith 'Fast upon seeing it and break upon seeing it' is cited. The imperative 'صوموا' indicates that the sighting creates a personal obligation to fast. Thus the individual must fast even if others do not.
This hadith is used to establish wajib fasting for the solitary sighting.
3
Examine the second proof (communal practice)
The hadith 'The fast is the day you fast, the breaking is the day you break' and the athar of Hasan al-Basri emphasize that communal practice governs the public celebration of Eid. Therefore, the individual cannot unilaterally break fast.
These proofs reconcile personal obligation with communal authority.
4
Understand the legal principle
The passage states a principle: one can act on personal certainty but cannot impose it on others without a judge's ruling or binding testimony. Hence the individual must follow the qadi's decision even if he is certain.
This is a key maxim in Hanafi fiqh: personal certainty does not override public authority in matters of communal worship.
5
Apply the consequence: no kaffarah
If the individual breaks his fast despite the ruling, he does not owe kaffarah because the qadi's rejection created a legitimate doubt (shubha) about the month. Only qada' (make-up) is required.
This differentiates Hanafi view from some other schools that impose kaffarah for willful violation.

Source Text

تشریح : اس عبارت کی تفصیل او پر گزر چکی ہے۔ یعنی جس نے عید کا چاند دیکھا اور قاضی نے نہیں مانا تو اپنے دیکھنے اور یقین
Chapter on what establishes the crescent. (1018) And it is not permissible for him to break fast based on his certainty of the crescent of Shawwal. Commentary: There are two issues: [1] A person saw the crescent of Ramadan but the judge did not accept his testimony and the common people did not fast, yet that person must fast because Ramadan is established for him due to his sighting; however, if he did not fast, no kaffarah is required because the judge's rejection caused Ramadan to become doubtful in his mind. [2] The second issue: A person saw the crescent of Eid and the judge did not accept his testimony; then it is not necessary for him to break fast; he must continue fasting because the ruling on Eid is determined by the judge so that the communal Eid prayer may be performed; therefore, since the judge did not decide, Eid has not occurred for him and it remains Ramadan, so he will fast. However, if he broke the fast, no kaffarah is necessary, because his sighting of the crescent caused Ramadan to become doubtful in his case. All these divisions apply when he actually saw the crescent, not if he is giving false testimony. Evidence: (1) For the one who sees the crescent, the proof for fasting is this hadith: 'I heard Abu Huraira say: The Prophet ﷺ said: Fast upon seeing it and break fast upon seeing it; if it is cloudy for you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty.' (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith indicates that since he has seen the crescent, he must fast even alone. (2) And to celebrate Eid with the people, the proof is this hadith: 'The fast is the day you fast, the breaking is the day you break, and the sacrifice is the day you sacrifice.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates to observe Ramadan, Eid, and Eid al-Adha with the people. (3) There is also the saying of a Tabi'i: 'He should not fast except with the people and should not break fast except with the people.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). Principle: If one is certain of something, he should act upon it, but he cannot impose it on others unless there is a judge's ruling or conclusive testimony. Translation: (1018) And it is not permissible for him to break fast based on his certainty of the crescent of Shawwal. Commentary: The explanation of this phrase has passed above. That is, the one who saw the crescent of Eid and the judge did not accept, due to his sighting and certainty [the text is cut].
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (1018) from the matn along with its proofs. The author begins by stating that a person who sees the Shawwal crescent on his own cannot break his fast based solely on his certainty if the judge has not accepted his testimony. The commentary in Urdu expands on two related scenarios: a person who sees the Ramadan crescent alone, and a person who sees the Shawwal crescent alone. In both cases, the individual must fast with the community, but if he breaks his fast, no kaffarah (expiation) is required because the judge's rejection creates doubt. The text then provides three proofs: (1) the hadith 'Fast upon seeing it...' which obligates fasting individually; (2) the hadith 'The fast is the day you fast...' which emphasizes communal practice; (3) the saying of Hasan al-Basri that one should fast and break only with the people. The principle stated is that one can act on personal certainty but cannot enforce it on others without a judge's ruling or binding testimony. This is a clear example of Hanafi reliance on both individual obligation and communal authority.

Key Terms
الهلال (al-hilal): The crescent of the new moon, used here specifically for the moons of Ramadan and Shawwal.
القاضي (al-qadi): The religious judge appointed by the Muslim authority; his decision on crescent sighting binds the community.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation required for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast without excuse. Here it is not required due to doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must break fast because he is certain of Eid.

C) He must break fast and pay kaffarah.
D) He may choose to fast or break.

Key Takeaway
A person who sees the Shawwal crescent alone must fast with the community; breaking due to certainty does not incur kaffarah.

Breaking Fast in Both Times: Qada' Required, No Kaffarah
Ruling on consequence of breaking fast due to personal crescent sighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who breaks fast based on personal crescent sighting and distinguish when qada' alone is required versus qada' plus kaffarah.

Core Idea
Doubt from judicial rejection lifts kaffarah but not qada'.

This ruling clarifies a specific scenario in the fiqh of fasting: what happens when someone's personal certainty about the moon sighting conflicts with the judge's decision. The source passage tells us that even if the person broke his fast before the judge's rejection, only a makeup fast (qada') is required, not the heavy expiation (kaffarah). Understanding the role of doubt in altering consequences is key to applying this correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
The act is breaking a fast – either by not fasting when Ramadan is believed to have started, or by breaking the fast when Eid is believed to have arrived – based on personal crescent sighting.
'Both times' refers to Ramadan time (when one should fast) and Shawwal time (when one should break).
2
Find the consequence
The matn states two consequences: 'qada' (make up the fast) and 'no kaffarah' (no expiation).
Qada' is an obligatory makeup fast; kaffarah is a severe expiation (e.g., fasting two months) reserved for deliberate violations.
3
Identify the condition that modifies the ruling
The condition is that the person relied on his own sighting, and the judge later rejects his testimony. Even if he broke before the rejection, the same ruling applies because the obligation becomes doubtful for him.
The key concept is shubha (doubt) – it prevents kaffarah.
4
Appreciate the underlying principle
In Hanafi fiqh, kaffarah is only wajib when the act is a clear, deliberate violation without any excuse. Doubt (even honest certainty that later conflicts with authority) removes the strictness.
This principle protects individuals from over-penalization when they act on sincere ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (١٠١٩) وان أفـطـر فـي الـوقـتـيـن قـضـى ولا كـفـارـة عـلـيـه ولو كان فطره قبل ما ردّه القاضي في الصحيح
تشریح : رمضان کا چاند دیکھنے والے کو رمضان کا روزہ رکھنا چاہئے ، اسی طرح عید کے چاند دیکھنے والے کو بھی عام لوگوں کے ساتھ روزہ رکھنا چاہئے لیکن نہیں رکھا تو کفارہ لازم نہیں ہو گا صرف قضا لازم ہوگی ، چاہے قاضی کے رد کرنے سے پہلے ہی روزہ توڑ دے تب بھی صحیح مسلک یہی ہے، کیونکہ اس کے حق میں مشکوک ہو گیا۔
لغت : فی وقتین : سے مراد رمضان کا وقت ، اور عید کا وقت ہے۔
Translation: (1019) And if he breaks his fast in both times, he must make it up and there is no expiation upon him, even if his breaking was before the judge rejected him, according to the correct view. Commentary: The one who sees the crescent of Ramadan must fast, and similarly the one who sees the crescent of Eid must fast with the people, but if he did not fast, no kaffarah is due; only qada' is required. Even if he broke his fast before the judge's rejection, the correct view is the same, because it became doubtful for him. Lexicon: 'In both times' refers to the time of Ramadan and the time of Eid.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage provides the legal consequence for a person who breaks his fast based on his personal sighting of the crescent, whether for Ramadan or Shawwal. The matn states that if he breaks fast in either of the two times (i.e., by not fasting when he should have, or by breaking when he should have continued), he must make up the fast (qada') but no expiation (kaffarah) is required. The commentary clarifies that this applies even if he broke his fast before the qadi had a chance to reject his testimony. The reason is that his personal certainty is undermined by the judge's authority, making the obligation doubtful. The vocabulary note explains that 'both times' means the time of Ramadan (when he should fast) and the time of Eid (when he should break with the community).

Key Terms
قضى (qada'): To make up a missed obligatory fast after the month.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation for intentional breaking of Ramadan fast without valid excuse, not required here due to doubt.
الوقتين (al-waqtayn): The two times: the time of Ramadan and the time of Shawwal (Eid).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Both qada' and kaffarah.
B) Qada' only, no kaffarah.
C) Kaffarah only, no qada'.
D) Nothing, because his personal certainty justified breaking.

Key Takeaway
Breaking fast based on personal crescent sighting that conflicts with judicial authority requires qada' but not kaffarah due to doubt.

Accepting One Witness for Crescent Sighting in Cloudy Weather
Ruling with evidence on crescent testimony in cloudy weather

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting one witness for crescent sighting when the sky is cloudy, explain the condition of the witness's integrity, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
When the sky is cloudy, the testimony of one trustworthy person suffices to establish the crescent.

In clear skies, the Hanafi school typically requires two witnesses for crescent sighting, but when visibility is obstructed by clouds, dust, or fog, the requirement is relaxed. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence, distinguishing between religious and transactional matters in witness requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The text specifies a hindrance ('illa) in the sky: clouds, dust, or similar. This is the key condition that triggers the relaxed ruling.
The existence of the hindrance is determined by the observer.
2
State the ruling
When the condition is met, the testimony of a single person—whether 'adl (righteous) or mastur (concealed status)—is accepted. 'Mastur' means his integrity is not publicly known but no sin is apparent.
A fasiq (open sinner) is not acceptable even in religious matters.
3
Examine the evidence
The text cites two hadith: Ibn Umar's report where the Prophet fasted and ordered others based on his sole testimony, and the Bedouin report where the Prophet accepted a single witness.
These hadith are ahad (single transmission), but sufficient for a religious ruling.
4
Cross-madhhab comparison
Some other schools require two witnesses even in cloudy conditions, treating it like a financial matter. Hanafis distinguish religious matters (ibadat) from mu'amalat, allowing one witness here.
This distinction is rooted in usul al-fiqh: religious matters rely more on certainty than quantity of witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (١٠٢٠) واذا كان بالسماء علّة من غيم او غبار او نحوه قبل خبر واحد عدل او مسرور في الصحيح
تشریح : آسمان میں علت یعنی افق پر غبار ہو، کہرا ہو یا بادل ہو تو ممکن ہے کہ کس کو چاند نظر آجائے اور کسی کو نظر نہ آئے اس لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی بھی قبول ہوگی ۔ معاملات کی گواہی کی طرح دو آدمی ہونا ضروری نہیں ، البتہ عادل ہو یا مستور الحال ہو کیونکہ دینی امور میں فاسق کی گواہی قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔
وجه (۱) چاند دیکھنے کا معاملہ امر دینی ہے۔ معاملات نہیں ہے اس لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی بھی قابل قبول ہے۔ اور تحمیل شہادت یعنی دو گواہی کی ضرورت نہیں (۲) عن ابن عمر قال تراءى الناس الهلال فأخبرت رسول الله له أني رأيته
فصام وأمر الناس بصيامه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فى شهادة الواحد علی رویت هلال رمضان ص ١٣٤١، نمبر ٢٣٤٢) اس حدیث میں ایک آدمی کی گواہی پر رمضان کا فیصلہ فرمایا۔ (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال جاء اعرابی الی النبی صلى الله عليه
فقال اني رايت الهلال قال الحسن في حديثه یعنی رمضان فقال اتشهد ان لا اله الا الله؟ قال نعم قال اتشهد ان محمدا رسول الله قال نعم قال يا بلال اذن فى الناس فليصوموا غدا (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في شهادة الواحد علی رویت هلال رمضان ، ص ٣٤١، نمبر ٢٣٤٠ ر ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصوم بالشہادة ، ص ١٧٦، نمبر (٦٩) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمضان کے ثبوت کے لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی کافی ہے۔
Translation: (1020) And if there is a hindrance in the sky such as clouds, dust, or the like, the report of one righteous (adl) or concealed (mastur) person is accepted, according to the correct view. Commentary: If there is a hindrance in the sky, i.e., dust on the horizon, fog, or clouds, it is possible that some may see the crescent and others not, so the testimony of one person will be accepted. It is not necessary to have two persons as in transactions; however, he must be righteous (adl) or of concealed status (mastur), because the testimony of a sinful person (fasiq) is not acceptable in religious matters. Evidence: (1) The matter of crescent sighting is a religious matter, not a transactional one, so the testimony of one person is acceptable, and the requirement of two witnesses is not needed. (2) Ibn Umar said: 'The people were looking for the crescent, and I informed the Messenger of Allah ﷺ that I had seen it, so he fasted and ordered the people to fast.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that a ruling was made based on the testimony of one person. (3) Ibn Abbas reported that a Bedouin came to the Prophet ﷺ and said he had seen the crescent (meaning Ramadan), and the Prophet asked him about his faith, then ordered Bilal to announce that the people should fast the next day. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that the testimony of one person is sufficient to establish Ramadan.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on accepting the testimony of a single person for crescent sighting when meteorological conditions are unfavorable (clouds, dust, fog). The commentary explains that since the matter is religious (dini), not transactional (mu'amalat), the standard requirement of two witnesses is waived. However, the witness must be 'adl (righteous) or mastur (of concealed status, i.e., whose integrity is not known but no known sin), as a fasiq (open sinner) is not acceptable. The text supports this with three proofs: (1) a rational argument that crescent sighting is a religious act; (2) the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet accepted his sole testimony; (3) the hadith of the Bedouin whose single report led the Prophet to declare a fast. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school, which distinguishes between religious and transactional matters in terms of witness requirements.

Key Terms
عدل ('adl): A person of known integrity and uprightness, whose testimony is accepted unconditionally.
مستور (mastur): A person whose religious status is concealed, i.e., not known to be sinful but not known to be upright either; their testimony is accepted in religious matters.
علة ('illa): A hindrance or obstacle in the sky preventing clear sighting, such as clouds, dust, fog.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The witness must be a relative of the qadi.
D) The testimony must be given in writing.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the testimony of one trustworthy person is accepted for crescent sighting when visibility is poor, based on prophetic practice.

Breaking Fast After a Contested Crescent Sighting
States ruling for breaking fast after claiming to see crescent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on breaking the fast after a contested crescent sighting and distinguish between qada and kaffarah in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Breaking fast on doubtful crescent sighting requires only qada, not kaffarah.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the chapter of fasting: a person claims to have seen the Ramadan or Eid crescent but breaks his fast before the judge's rejection. The Hanafi school rules that only qada is owed, not kaffarah, due to the doubt (shubha) created by the judicial overruling. Understanding this ruling clarifies the conditions under which kaffarah applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal context
The person claims to see the crescent (Ramadan or Eid) and breaks his fast before the judge rejects his claim. Consider the hukm of breaking the fast in this case.
The act is breaking an assumed obligatory fast based on a personal sighting.
2
Determine the required actions
The school mandates qada (make-up) but not kaffarah (expiation). Note the difference: qada compensates the missed worship; kaffarah is an additional penalty for intentional violation without doubt.
Qada is wajib; kaffarah is not due.
3
Understand the legal cause (sabab) for the reduced penalty
The judge's rejection creates doubt (shubha) about the obligation of the fast. In Hanafi law, kaffarah is only imposed when the violation is certain and without excuse.
Shubha removes kaffarah but not qada, because the fast was physically broken.
4
Apply the ruling to both contexts
The ruling covers both Ramadan and Eid crescent situations. The principle is the same: the individual must follow the community and make up any fast broken due to an uncorroborated sighting.
This underscores the communal nature of fasting and the authority of the qadi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فيما يثبت به الهلال (۱۰۱۹) وان أفـطـر فـي الـوقـتـيـن قـضـى ولا كـفـارـة عـلـيـه ولو كان فطره قبل ما ردّه القاضي في الصحيح

كرنے کی وجہ سے یہ آدمی روزہ نہ توڑے، بلکہ روزہ رکھے اور اگلے دن سب کے ساتھ عید کرے کیونکہ عید سب کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۰۱۹) اور اگر دونوں وقتوں ( رمضان و عید کا چاند دیکھ کر ) افطار کر لیا تو اس پر قضا ہے کفارہ نہیں اگر چہ اس نے افطار کر لیا قاضی کے رد کرنے سے پہلے پیج مسلک میں۔ تشریح : رمضان کا چاند دیکھنے والے کو رمضان کا روزہ رکھنا چاہئے ، اسی طرح عید کے چاند دیکھنے والے کو بھی عام لوگوں کے ساتھ روزہ رکھنا چاہئے لیکن نہیں رکھا تو کفارہ لازم نہیں ہو گا صرف قضا لازم ہوگی ، چاہے قاضی کے رد کرنے سے پہلے ہی روزہ توڑ دے تب بھی صحیح مسلک یہی ہے، کیونکہ اس کے حق میں مشکوک ہو گیا۔

لغت : فی وقتین : سے مراد رمضان کا وقت ، اور عید کا وقت ہے۔
Section on what establishes the crescent. (1019) And if he broke his fast in both times, he must make up and there is no expiation upon him, even if his breaking was before the judge rejected it, according to the correct view. Because of this, this person should not break his fast, but keep it and the next day celebrate Eid with everyone, since Eid is with everyone. Translation (1019): And if he broke the fast in both times (after seeing the crescent of Ramadan and Eid), then upon him is qada, no kaffarah, even if he broke the fast before the judge rejected it, in the correct school. Explanation: The one who sees the crescent of Ramadan must fast, and likewise the one who sees the crescent of Eid must fast with the people, but if he did not, then no kaffarah, only qada is necessary, even if he broke the fast before the judge's rejection, this is the correct school, because it became doubtful for him. Lexicon: 'fi waqtayn' means the time of Ramadan and the time of Eid.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Thamaratun Najah on the consequence of breaking the fast after claiming to see the crescent of Ramadan or Eid. According to the Hanafi school, a person who sights the crescent of Ramadan must fast that day, and one who sights the crescent of Eid must not break his fast until the people collectively break. If the person breaks his fast, his claim is typically rejected by the judge due to public consensus, and because of the doubt (shubha) arising from the rejection, the obligation of the fast becomes uncertain. Therefore, only qada (making up the missed fast) is required, not kaffarah (expiation). This is the relied-upon (sahih) position in the school. The lexicon explains that 'both times' refers to the time of Ramadan and the time of Eid.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory fast on a later day.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast without excuse; not required here.
الوقتين (al-waqtayn): Both times: Ramadan and Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qada and kaffarah
B) Qada only
C) No penalty
D) Kaffarah only

Key Takeaway
When doubt (shubha) is introduced by judicial rejection of a crescent claim, only qada is required, not kaffarah.

Single Witness for Crescent in Cloudy Skies
States ruling and proof for single witness when sky is obstructed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on crescent testimony when sky is obstructed and identify the conditions that make a single witness acceptable.

Core Idea
One just or concealed witness suffices for Ramadan when clouds block the sky.

Crescent sighting is a religious duty that marks the start of Ramadan. But what if the sky is cloudy? The Hanafi school, drawing on prophetic practice, eases the usual two-witness requirement. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling's trigger condition
The ruling applies only when the sky has an obstruction ('illah): clouds, dust, or similar. Determine if the condition is present before considering the witness requirement.
Without obstruction, the normal rule of two witnesses applies.
2
Specify the acceptable witnesses
The ruling accepts two categories: 'adil (just) and mastur (concealed but upright). Understand the difference and why mastur suffices here but not in hudud.
Mastur: person whose inner state is unknown but appears Muslim and honest.
3
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas. Read them and note how the Prophet accepted a single report and acted on it.
Both hadith are ahad (single narrated) but deemed reliable for this ruling.
4
Apply the principle of 'amr dini
The text explains that crescent sighting is a religious matter (amr dini), not a transaction (mu'amili). This relaxes the requirement of two witnesses. Understand the distinction.
In transactions, two men or one man and two women are normally needed.
5
Contrast with other schools
Some schools require two witnesses even when sky is cloudy. Note the Hanafi reliance on hadith and the principle of facilitation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences for Ramadan start.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۰۲۰) واذا كان بالسماء علّة من غيم او غبار او نحوه قبل . خبر واحد عدل او مسرور في الصحيح

تشریح : آسمان میں علت یعنی افق پر غبار ہو، کہرا ہو یا بادل ہو تو ممکن ہے کہ کس کو چاند نظر آجائے اور کسی کو نظر نہ آئے اس لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی بھی قبول ہوگی ۔ معاملات کی گواہی کی طرح دو آدمی ہونا ضروری نہیں ، البتہ عادل ہو یا مستور الحال ہو کیونکہ دینی امور میں فاسق کی گواہی قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔

وجه (۱) چاند دیکھنے کا معاملہ امر دینی ہے۔ معاملات نہیں ہے اس لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی بھی قابل قبول ہے۔ اور تحمیل شہادت یعنی دو گواہی کی ضرورت نہیں (۲) عن ابن عمر قال تراءى الناس الهلال فأخبرت رسول الله له أني رأيته فصام وأمر الناس بصيامه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فى شهادة الواحد علی رویت هلال رمضان ص ۱۳۴۱، نمبر ۲۳۴۲) اس حدیث میں ایک آدمی کی گواہی پر رمضان کا فیصلہ فرمایا۔ (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال جاء اعرابی الی النبی صلى الله فقال اني رايت الهلال قال الحسن في حديثه یعنی رمضان فقال اتشهد ان لا اله الا الله؟ قال نعم قال اتشهد ان محمدا رسول الله قال نعم قال يا بلال اذن فى الناس فليصوموا غدا (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في شهادة الواحد علی رویت هلال رمضان ، ص ۳۴۱، نمبر ۲۳۴۰ ر ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصوم بالشہادة ، ص ۱۷۶، نمبر (۶۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمضان کے ثبوت کے لئے ایک آدمی کی گواہی کافی ہے۔
Translation (1020): And if there is in the sky an obstruction from clouds or dust or the like, the news of one upright or concealed person is accepted, according to the correct view. Explanation: If there is an obstruction on the horizon like dust, fog, or clouds, it is possible that some see the crescent and others do not; therefore the testimony of one person is accepted. It is not necessary to have two like in transactions; as long as the person is upright or concealed, because in religious matters the testimony of a sinner is not acceptable. Evidence (1): The matter of sighting the crescent is a religious matter, not a transactional one, so the testimony of one person is acceptable, and there is no need for imposing the condition of two witnesses. (2) From Ibn Umar: The people were looking for the crescent, so I informed the Messenger of Allah that I had seen it, so he fasted and ordered the people to fast. (Abu Dawud, chapter on testimony of one for Ramadan crescent, p.1341, no.2342) In this hadith, a decision was made based on one person's testimony. (3) In a hadith: From Ibn Abbas: A bedouin came to the Prophet and said 'I have seen the crescent.' al-Hasan (in his narration) said 'i.e., of Ramadan.' So he said 'Do you testify that there is no god but Allah?' He said 'Yes.' He said 'Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah?' He said 'Yes.' He said 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast tomorrow.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on testimony of one for Ramadan crescent, p.341, no.2340; Tirmidhi, chapter on fasting with testimony, p.176, no.69) From this hadith it is known that one person's testimony is sufficient for establishing Ramadan.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. It states the Hanafi position that when the sky is cloudy or dusty, a single 'adil (just) or mastur (concealed, i.e., of unknown but outwardly upright character) person's report is sufficient to establish the sighting of the Ramadan crescent. The reason given is that this is a religious matter (amr dini), not a transaction (mu'amili), so strict conditions of two witnesses are relaxed. The author adduces two hadith: that of Ibn Umar and that of Ibn Abbas, both showing the Prophet accepting testimony of one person for Ramadan. This establishes that for Ramadan, one witness is enough; for Eid, the conditions differ as seen later.

Key Terms
علة (illah): Obstruction in the sky such as clouds, dust, or fog that hinders sighting.
مستور (mastur): A person whose inner state is unknown but appears upright; their testimony is accepted in religious matters.
عدل (adl): A just, upright person whose testimony is inherently reliable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, when the sky is cloudy, how many witnesses are required to confirm the Ramadan crescent?
A) Two just men
B) One just or concealed person
C) Two men or one man and two women
D) Four witnesses

Key Takeaway
When atmospheric obstruction hinders sighting, a single reliable witness suffices for Ramadan crescent in the Hanafi school.
